SADC is off target interms of integration agenda, there is a need to redraw the integration calender.
Regional integration is SADC is not going to be easy but it is a goal worth pursuing for the benefits of our economies and our people.
Regional integration is about weaving and tying economies together.It is the way to go for SADC in upscalling regional economic integration.
SADC has achieved more in terms of regional cooperation but so much need to be done on the side of regional integration.
In going forward, there is a need for SADC to distinguish between Regional Cooperation and Regional Integration.
Critical to upscalling the regional integration in SADC is investment in soft and hard infrastructure.

SADCC founding fathers realized individually their countries are small and weak but collectively a region can become formidable power house

The Commonwealth urge all political parties and candidates in Zambia to respect the will of the people of Zambia
Zambia has a history of upholding democratic values during elections. We urge all stakeholders to cherish this history.
We noted, where there were anomalies, they were not of such gravity as to negatively impact the credibility of the process.
We appeal to all Zambians to refrain from making any utterances and acts that could trigger tensions and affect post election enviroment
Urge all parties and candidates in Zambia to seek redress for any grievances through peaceful dialogue and through prescribed legal channels
It is our hope and expactation that the spirit of orderliness,tolerance and peace, which has characterized the voting process will prevail
Mindful that results process is ongoing, our final assessment on the entire process will be contained in our final report @commonwealthsec
Our overall conclusion is that the voting,closing and counting process at the polling stations were credible and transparent.
Challenges obseved, inadequate education on the referendum, queue managenent and late opening of the few polling stations
We have witnessed an encouraging turn-out,a largely peaceful process, a robust voter register and non intrusive presence of police
Most voting stations opened on time with few exceptions. We were strucked by very long queues in some polling stations.
It is view of stakeholders that media in Zambia is polarised. Both public and private media have in some cases reported events innacurately
I am about to present Commonwealth Observer Group Interim Statement forn Zambia General Elections

Way forward Panel recommends calling of High Level Summit on Global Public Health Crises in 2018.
Way forward Panel recommends the establishment of a High-Level Council on Global Public Health Crises
Without a dramatic attitudinal change in the global health architecture,the world may be in a similar or even worse situation in next crisis
Panel has recommended the establishment of a fund of at least US$1 billion for research and development on priority communicable diseases
The Ebola outbreak was difficult to control causing many deaths as a result, because there was no vaccine nor medicine.
The WHO Contingency Fund to be increased to $300 million instead of the proposed $100 million by Member States based on assessed scale.
Panel proposes 10% of voluntary contributions to the WHO to be directed to building operational capacity.
To ensure finances for WHO,Panel proposes Member states statutory contribution be increased by 10 percent to be dedicated for this purpose
The Panel, further proposes that the Centre should have own Advisory Board to give it the necessary levels of operational autonomy.
Panel welcomes the decision taken by the Director General of WHO to establish a Centre for Emergency Preparedness and Response.
If WHO is to perform emergence and operational functions,i t must be reformed and credible operational and emergence capacity be built.
The Panel is convinced, that there is no substitute to the World Health Organization as the single global leader on health matters.
WHO relies on voluntary contributions by countries, orgzs and persons of good will to undertake and underwrite the response.
WHO doesnt have the financial,technical and human resources to undertake& coordinate a strong response on its own during major outbreak.
The WHO lacks operational capacity and the little that there was has been almost crippled by lack of funding.
WHO could not live up to expectation it is more of a normative institution and not an operational one.
Panel is proposing a joint meeting between WHO and the WTO to discuss ways to adress airline responces to future health crises
It was not wise for the WHO to delay declaration of a PHEIC. In future, the WHO should go ahead and do what is the right
Panel recommends in future outbreaks, the WHO should not wait until many people have died to cause a credible response to be mounted.
The outbreak was first reported Dec 2013 whereas the PHEIC was declared in Aug, 2014.
The WHO was slow in declaring a Public Health Emergency of International Concern (Pheic)
Global response was too slow and inadequate for the Ebola outbreak in West Africa. Many lives were lost because of that.
Panel recommends regional orgz build response capacities ready to be deployed in the event of a health crisis within their regions.
The deployment of medical professionals and the mobilisation of govts and the private sector to contribute resources were good examples
Panel was impressed with the contributions of both the @_AfricanUnion and the ECOWAS in the fight against Ebola.
Smooth functioning of coordination structures, understanding of the cultures and respect thereof are critical elements of the response.
Panel advise in future outbreaks & responses, governance and effective community engagement by the responders should be given high priority.
governance as well as knowledge of the disease and the culture of the local communities were critical for the success of the response.
Out of $ 30 billion spent annually by donors, bulk goes to disease control and eradication programmes and not strengthening health systems
Panel recommends donor countries give serious consideration to supporting developing countries to build IHR core capacities & health systems
Ways must be found to ensure that all countries are fully IHR compliant by 2020.
Sadly, though a binding obligation only 65 out of 196 State Parties to IHR have met the minimum core capacities standards
The Panel learnt that most WHO member states are not compliant with the requirements of the International Health Regulations (IHR).
In 2013, for example, Guinea had 1 doctor per 10,000 people, Liberia and Sierra Leone had 0.2 and 0.1. The WHO standard is 23 per 10,000.
The Panel learnt that in many developing nations health systems are weak,they make these countries vulnerable to outbreaks of diseases.
If deficiencies are not addressed, in the outbreak of any other pandemic in the developing world the consequences would be even more severe.
The Ebola crisis laid bare the serious weaknesses or inadequacy of the international health architecture at the national,regional and global
Tourism suffered much through cancellation of bookings for the so called fear of Ebola in the whole of African continent.
Even African countries that were very far away from the three countries were adversely affected by Ebola crisis
As a result of Ebola crisis, World Bank estimates a $ 2.2 billion loss to GDP of the three countries Liberia,Guinea and Sierra Leone
The Panel learnt a lot the challenges faced during the Ebola crisis and about the national, regional and international efforts and responses
Will share the Key Findings and Recommendations of the Panel I chaired on Global Responce to Health Crises from Dakar via video conference
I thanks @UN_PGA for invitation to participate on the Briefing on the Implementation of the Recommendations of the Panel on Health Crisis

Tumeipatia TADB uongozi mahiri. Kilimo ni kazi na ni shughuli ya kibiashara, siyo shughuli ya watu waliokosa kazi na fursa ya kwenda mjini.
TADB itatumia mabenki ya biashara yaliyopo kuwafikia wakulima kwa masharti mahsusi ya Benki ya Maendeleo ya Kilimo.
Benki hii itafadhili miradi ya kilimo na ile inayochochea kilimo katika mnyororo wa thamani wa kilimo; kwa kuanzia benki haitapokea amana.
Tofauti na benki za biashara, TADB shughuli yake kilimo. Lengo ni kuwakopesha wakulima na vikundi vya wakulima kwa masharti nafuu.
Agosti 8 tulizindua Benki ya Maendeleo ya Kilimo (TADB) kwa mtaji wa shilingi bilioni 60. Lengo ni kufikia bilioni 800 katika miaka 8 ijayo.
Leo ni Siku ya Vijana Duniani. Tutie nia kuendelea kuchagua viongozi weledi na watakaotambua nafasi ya vijana katika jamii na kuisimamia.

Tunaimarisha ustawi kwa namna mbili. 1. Kuboresha huduma kwa wananchi kwenye elimu, afya na miundombinu. Hii ni changamoto tunayofanikiwa.
